    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_db0c11ac-0612-4909-a54d-d09eb825a51f'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer7049544414122164673">Harold Gaynor offers Anita Blake a million dollars to raise a 300-year-old zombie. Knowing it means a human sacrifice will be necessary, Anita turns him down. But when dead bodies start turning up, she realizes that someone else has raised Harold's zombie--and that the zombie is a killer. Anita pits her power against the zombie and the voodoo priestess who controls it.<br/><br/>In <i>T</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7049544414122164673" style="display:none">Harold Gaynor offers Anita Blake a million dollars to raise a 300-year-old zombie. Knowing it means a human sacrifice will be necessary, Anita turns him down. But when dead bodies start turning up, she realizes that someone else has raised Harold's zombie--and that the zombie is a killer. Anita pits her power against the zombie and the voodoo priestess who controls it.<br /><br />In <i>The Laughing Corpse</i> Anita will learn that there are some secrets better left buried-and some people better off dead...</span>

        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063030731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2185297284692678982"><i>”Your eyes are the clearest mirror I have ever seen, ma petite. Whenever I begin to pretend to myself. Whenever I have delusions of life. I have only to look into your face and see the truth.”<br/>What did he expect me to say? Sorry, I’ll try to ignore the fact that you’re a vampire. “So why keep me around?” I asked.<br/>“Perhaps if Nikolaos had had such a mirror, she would not have been such a monster.”</i><br/><br/>It’s been quite a while I read the first book of this series and I’m glad that I remembered to pick up </span>
  <span id="freeText2185297284692678982" style="display:none"><i>”Your eyes are the clearest mirror I have ever seen, ma petite. Whenever I begin to pretend to myself. Whenever I have delusions of life. I have only to look into your face and see the truth.”<br />What did he expect me to say? Sorry, I’ll try to ignore the fact that you’re a vampire. “So why keep me around?” I asked.<br />“Perhaps if Nikolaos had had such a mirror, she would not have been such a monster.”</i><br /><br />It’s been quite a while I read the first book of this series and I’m glad that I remembered to pick up book two because I’m pretty certain this series is going to be some sort of “guilty pleasure” of mine. *lol* <br /><br />I mean what’s not to love?<br /><br />- A kickass heroine that might be small in size but is freaking damn powerful and scary<br />- A good portion of weird humour<br />- Necromancers, animators, voodoo priestesses, human sacrifices, zombies, vampires, … the list could go on and on!<br />- Jean-Claude!!! (To be honest he’s one of the main reasons. After all I love myself some mysterious dark vampire. *yummy*) <br />- Easy banter between the characters.<br /><i>”No, no,” Dolph said. “You two in a car alone. Only one of you would come out alive.”<br />“And it’d be me,” I said.<br />Zerbrowski nodded. “Ain’t it the truth.”</i> <br />*LOL* For some reason that made me like Zerbrowski even more. Haha! <br />- Dark, dark, dark as well as bloody and gory content. <br /><br />So this said I’m pretty sure I won’t wait another 3 years until I pick up book 3! ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="2185297284692678982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421530028" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421530028" />
    <a title="Meredith Holley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley"><img alt="Meredith Holley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548641865p2/1302775.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421530028?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith Holley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith Holley" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley">Meredith Holley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143144021" href="/book/show/6399684-the-laughing-corpse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=disturbing">disturbing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=shiving-tour">shiving-tour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=chosen-girls">chosen-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=motherless-daughters">motherless-daughters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421530028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18391434399143049412">This was TERRIBLE. Terrible!!! Why are you here book??? Why do you exist?? Why do you suck SO MUCH??? Ugh!! I was listening to this while walking to work in the morning, and I’m pretty sure I was waking up whole neighborhoods with my loud, “UGGGGHHHHHHH”s because I could not refrain from reacting to what a bitch this book is. This book is such a little bitch. It is not SO bad to start out with, just your normal Anita Blake bitchiness, like, “girls shouldn’t wear pink; girls shouldn’t shop; girls</span>
  <span id="freeText18391434399143049412" style="display:none">This was TERRIBLE. Terrible!!! Why are you here book??? Why do you exist?? Why do you suck SO MUCH??? Ugh!! I was listening to this while walking to work in the morning, and I’m pretty sure I was waking up whole neighborhoods with my loud, “UGGGGHHHHHHH”s because I could not refrain from reacting to what a bitch this book is. This book is such a little bitch. It is not SO bad to start out with, just your normal Anita Blake bitchiness, like, “girls shouldn’t wear pink; girls shouldn’t shop; girls shouldn’t be feminine; girls shouldn’t like boys.” And then the boys like her sooooo much because she is such an asshole. So, don’t worry, slatherings of male approval if you don’t wear pink.<br><br>OH MY GOD. UGGGGGHHHHH.<br><br>And THEN, after you trudge through Anita’s complete lack of personality and LAME sense of humor, why not throw on some racism, homophobia, and a huge helping of ableism? WHY THE FUCK NOT?? UGGGHHH. I want to punch this book in its smug little curly-haired kisser. It makes me figuratively puke. <br><br>According to people who have read beyond this book, at some point, Anita starts having sex with random monsters, which . . . whatever. I don’t even care about that because she is so obnoxiously prudish in these first two books. And, the thing is, if you don’t want to have sex with a vampire, more power to ya girl. But THEN the simpering self-congratulation about it. It makes me crazy. You suck so much, Anita Blake. You are everything wrong about anything to do with gender.<br><br>I figure there are numerous ways women can react to sexism when they realize it is there, so I’ve made a little chart to illustrate my thoughts on the matter:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>As you can see, in my mind, all choices except doing whatever the fuck you want lead to a woman’s life being basically sacrificed to sexism. And this probably works the same with masculinity, too, obvs. I feel like I've forgotten another manifestation of women accepting sexism that looks almost like feminism, but I can't think what it is. And Anita Blake, all through this stupid book, is calling herself a feminist. You know she's a feminist because all the boys think she a spunky little hottie. Puke. This fake bullshit is such an easy justification for people saying they aren't feminists. But, how can you say anything is feminist that hates women and only seeks male approval? Puke.<br><br>On the one hand, I am so grateful to the women who came before me and forced people to recognize their skills and abilities so that hopefully in the future this stupid conversation will never even happen. So grateful. On the other hand, I think it is disgusting that the lives of capable women are sacrifices to either some kind of awkward attempt to be men or to a fight for the mere survival of girls because they are girls. I would consider someone like Lisbeth Salander an example of a woman who is painful to read about because her life is totally sacrifice to the mere survival of women. I don't think that's bad on Lisbeth's part, just depressing. I would consider Anita Blake a grotesque caricature of a woman trying to prove she is a man. Ugh. So uncomfortable to watch and annoying to hear about. Dude, just let girls wear pink if they want to wear pink. Pink is just a color, so dislike it if you want; but, also, pink is our childhood. And girlhood is not bad, so to the extent pink symbolizes women at our most innocently feminine, it pains me to hear women criticize it with the weight of rejecting their own innocent femininity. Again, like or dislike pink. Whatever you want. But, there is nothing noble or professional about hating the decorations of girlhood.<br><br>Aside from that, oh my god, the ableism in this book is absolutely disgusting. There is this whole section about a prostitute in a wheelchair, and Anita is like, “OH MY! KINKY! That is disgusting that anyone would want to have sex with a woman in a wheelchair!” No, you are disgusting, Anita Blake.<br><br>This is totally just a personal pet peeve, but it also really, really annoyed me the way Hamilton imagined being hardened to crime. Anita is hardened to crime here, so that means that she tosses around body parts at a crime scene and dares police officers not to puke in a room where the carpet is soaked in blood.<br><br>(Sidebar: it only really bothers her when she sees the dead bodies of children. Which, okay, I agree that it is, for whatever reason, exponentially more disturbing to hear about violence to children than adults. In a room soaked in blood, however, it strikes me as weird that she would not be bothered at all by a police officer jiggling a boob attached to a bloody rib cage, but a child’s hand would make her swoon.)<br><br>I have been privy to some pretty hilarious I-work-in-the-criminal-justice-system jokes lately, and, here, Hamilton did not even come close to what those sound like. Because they are only funny if they are respectful, if they have some kind of hope that some good will come of all of the criminal justice bullshit. This was so disrespectful. Not even close to funny. <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qlZGguSrp18" rel="nofollow noopener">This link is totally NSFW, but it is How You Do criminal justice system investigation comedy</a>. Hamilton's jokes are stupid, and her protagonist is stupider, and her snotty attitude about everyone who isn’t a 5’3”, 107 lb., curly-haired sprite is stupidest. Gross. UGGGHHHH. I hate you, book.<br><br>The audio reader was still good, though. I don't know how she managed reading this whole series. Voice of steel. Ugh, puke again on behalf of the poor reader.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18391434399143049412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1431265783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1431265783" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1431265783?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1431265783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11068620104994336287">When I read the Kate Daniels series, I would see a lot of reviews that compared her to Anita Blake, and Kate would always come out on top. I could see some similarities, obviously, but I find Anita a little disappointing in how dumb she is. She really doesn't know how to shut the hell up so that someone would NOT want to kill her for a change. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>"I'm going to kill you," he hissed.<br/>"Take a number," I said.</b>
</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446537195i/16827008.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>She'll need to buy more number machines if she keeps up this pace of pissing people off...</i><br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText11068620104994336287" style="display:none">When I read the Kate Daniels series, I would see a lot of reviews that compared her to Anita Blake, and Kate would always come out on top. I could see some similarities, obviously, but I find Anita a little disappointing in how dumb she is. She really doesn't know how to shut the hell up so that someone would NOT want to kill her for a change. <br><br><i>
  <b>"I'm going to kill you," he hissed.<br>"Take a number," I said.</b>
</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446537195i/16827008.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>She'll need to buy more number machines if she keeps up this pace of pissing people off...</i><br><br>I mean, seriously, this woman threatens and antagonizes everyone she meets. It just isn't smart. Can't she just simmer with rage and kill people in her head like the rest of us do?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446537195i/16827009.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> now, that's a healthy attitude!</i><br><br>So, in this book, there are a boatload of people who want to kill Anita. She's trying to help the police with a murder investigation and her standard way of interviewing people goes along the lines of this: <br><br>Anita: "Did you kill people?" <br><br>Person: "no". <br><br>Anita: "Well, I think you are a terrible person and should die, so I will be killing you as soon as possible." <br><br>Person: "Not if I kill you first."<br><br>Anita:"Did I mention that you are ugly and that I had sex with your mother? Also, I'm going to kill you."<br><br>Person: "Alright this is getting personal, now I'm going to torture you and then kill you."<br><br>Anita: "I'd like to see you try, bitch!"<br><br>Person: "Lady, I'm just trying to take your order. Do you want fries with that or not?"<br><br>And, then she is shocked when people keep trying to kill her! In this book, an old Voodoo lady tells her straight out that she is going to send a zombie to Anita's house to attack her while she sleeps that night. That night, lo and behold, a zombie tries to kill her. Then, Anita acts all shocked about it. That seems a little dumb to me. I mean, the lady was pretty clear on the plan. It really shouldn't have been shocking at all. I think that Anita has so many people telling her they are going to kill her each day that she can't keep up with all of the threats. She needs one of those day-planners to keep track. That's what they had back in the 90's right? When people still had to use pen &amp; paper for stuff. Fucking barbaric!<br><br>Anyway, I have to say, despite it all, I am still entertained. I'm going to go on to the next book to see how many people try to kill Anita in that one. Also, I'm intrigued by her fashion sense. Don't worry, I will be discussing that in greater detail in my next review. There has been mention of a fanny-pack. That is just too good to devote only a sentence or two on. It deserves the star treatment in my next review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11068620104994336287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2335422442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2335422442" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2335422442?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780515134445" href="/book/show/685372.The_Laughing_Corpse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2335422442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3544347620429658807">Anita got an offer to raise an ancient dead body as a zombie. The corpse is so old the only sacrifice sufficient to the occasion is a human one. Anita refused an got plenty of troubles as a result. At the same time something undead kept killing people wholesale and Anita, being a part of police Spook Squad had to find culprit and lay it to final rest as well as get the creature's creator. During her investigation she managed to piss off a powerful voodoo priestess and got plenty of troubles as a</span>
  <span id="freeText3544347620429658807" style="display:none">Anita got an offer to raise an ancient dead body as a zombie. The corpse is so old the only sacrifice sufficient to the occasion is a human one. Anita refused an got plenty of troubles as a result. At the same time something undead kept killing people wholesale and Anita, being a part of police Spook Squad had to find culprit and lay it to final rest as well as get the creature's creator. During her investigation she managed to piss off a powerful voodoo priestess and got plenty of troubles as a result. At the same time the Master vampire of the city unsuccessfully tried to get a date with her. Failing his wish could result in (you guessed it) plenty of troubles. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525043152i/25454716.png" alt="Troubles" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is better than the first one. The stupid parts of the plot are gone - almost. Also gone are boring characters: I am looking at you, Edward. The plot was moving with decent speed never leaving me bored. There were some genuinely creepy moments as well as gruesome ones. The latter showed me I became immune to such: modern news took care of it. Name me any day and I will find more sickening stuff in real life than a description of a bloody toddler parts scattered around.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525042997i/25454711._SX540_.jpg" alt="News" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>We - humans - suck and can be very sick. <br><br>One minor nitpick I would like to mention: for a self-proclaimed Vampire Executioner Anita did not do a whole lot of vampire executions this time (so you have no reason to worry, Buffy). <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525042873i/25454706._SX540_.png" alt="Buffy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This might be a good thing as vampire suck - both literally and figuratively. Figuratively speaking I think they overstayed their welcome in popular culture: sparkling and non-sparkling kind. <br><br>By the way in case anybody doubt Anita Blake is an ancestor of Kate Daniels: one scene in this book has strong resemblance of that in Magic Binds. I am talking about the scene of Anita trying on a bridesmaid dress. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525042681i/25454684._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="Bridesmaid dress" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I liked the book well enough to rate it with 4 stars. Your mileage may vary. To each his (her) own. Tastes differ; I am even willing to admit my taste in literature in non-existent. And so on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3544347620429658807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17022791143208303638">There was something about Hamilton's first, then second book that irritated the hell out of me, but I couldn't quite figure it out. Then one day I saw a picture of her on the book and I understood what it was. It annoys me when authors make themselves the hero/ine of their books, and then just change the name and the environment to make it fantasy fiction. But even more so when you must keep reading about how powerful, and how unconsciously sexy, and how tough that character is (*why* is she try</span>
  <span id="freeText17022791143208303638" style="display:none">There was something about Hamilton's first, then second book that irritated the hell out of me, but I couldn't quite figure it out. Then one day I saw a picture of her on the book and I understood what it was. It annoys me when authors make themselves the hero/ine of their books, and then just change the name and the environment to make it fantasy fiction. But even more so when you must keep reading about how powerful, and how unconsciously sexy, and how tough that character is (*why* is she trying to prove how gutsy she is to other male officers..by playing around with a dead baby's body parts?). What flaws she does have are laughable - like I care that she *almost* gave in to Jean the vampire's advances despite her no-sex-til-marriage vow.<br /><br />Maybe subsequent books get better.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1783959176000117712">I like these books. They are fun and entertaining. I like the MC, Anita. There certainly are character traits that annoy me about her, but they aren't deal breakers. I can't ever take this type of urban fantasy seriously. But with that said, the author has a way with words in her descriptive strokes. Sometimes it has me rolling my eyes, but mostly she does a great job of taking descriptions and adding layers to them. That is what I like the most. This is the 3rd book I've read by her and I have </span>
  <span id="freeText1783959176000117712" style="display:none">I like these books. They are fun and entertaining. I like the MC, Anita. There certainly are character traits that annoy me about her, but they aren't deal breakers. I can't ever take this type of urban fantasy seriously. But with that said, the author has a way with words in her descriptive strokes. Sometimes it has me rolling my eyes, but mostly she does a great job of taking descriptions and adding layers to them. That is what I like the most. This is the 3rd book I've read by her and I have thought this same thing about each of them.<br /><br />So far, the entertainment value of these are fairly high, but I have to say the same thing about the negative reviews. They are a riot to read. I laugh because I actually agree with their grievances, but apparently it hasn't sucked the joy out of these books....at least not yet anyway.</span>

<div id="review_228033034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228033034" />
    <a title="Tilly Slaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6289182-tilly-slaton"><img alt="Tilly Slaton" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228033034?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tilly Slaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tilly Slaton" href="/user/show/6289182-tilly-slaton">Tilly Slaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6289182-tilly-slaton?shelf=reviews-completed">reviews-completed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228033034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5182589141620054560">This book took my by surprise!<br/> <br/>I have read it twice now, and there are parts that are still heart-wrenching. <br/> <br/>In the second book of the Anita Blake series, The Laughing Corpse rips you from reality and tosses you unexpectedly into a world of voodoo, betrayal and forced submission.<br/> <br/>Following the first book, this begins centered around Anita Blake and her job as an animator as well as the consulting work she does for the paranormal police division that investigates homocides that are obviously per</span>
  <span id="freeText5182589141620054560" style="display:none">This book took my by surprise!<br /> <br />I have read it twice now, and there are parts that are still heart-wrenching. <br /> <br />In the second book of the Anita Blake series, The Laughing Corpse rips you from reality and tosses you unexpectedly into a world of voodoo, betrayal and forced submission.<br /> <br />Following the first book, this begins centered around Anita Blake and her job as an animator as well as the consulting work she does for the paranormal police division that investigates homocides that are obviously performed by something other than human.<br /> <br />The murder scenes are quite gruesome. I found myself continuing to hold my breath while my heart pounded in my chest. Almost saying to myself .. “Oh nono please ..” And reading as quickly as possible to find out if what I was dreading would be true.<br /> <br />Anita is confronted by an old voo doo priestess that scares the living hell out of anyone nearby, and even those whom feel they are unreachable. Safe. Unfortunately, sleeping in bed, quietly and feeling safe, relaxed .. the nightmares can still find you. Death can still come crawling through your windows.<br /> <br />The twists of betrayal, and sudden insights of a friend that leaves Anita unsure if the friendship will continue. Other friends are forced into life or death decisions, forced to consider crossing their moral lines of what is and what is not acceptable.<br /> <br />The end of the book was somewhat rushed, and as climatic as it was .. I was left wanting. Cliff hangers are a wonderful thing I suppose, but I wanted more. I wanted so much more than what the ending offered me. <br /> <br />Kudos to the author, I’m 1/4 into the next book <br /><br />I recommend this read to anyone interested in bloody and gruesome books that are centered around the paranormal and the slight progression of possible romantic relationships.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5182589141620054560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780441000913" href="/book/show/1044430.The_Laughing_Corpse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8101737-peter-tillman?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8101737-peter-tillman?shelf=friend-recos">friend-recos</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966716563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16545144716344204304">I'd been hesitant to read one of these, despite rave reviews by people I trust - I'm not much of a fantasy reader, & we're talking vampires, zombies and werewolves here. Well, folks, what we *really* have is a book in the class of the Harold Shea books - one that bends genres and transcends them. I'm not even really going to review the book . . . .<br/><br/>Let me back off a moment, & tell you what I usually read. I'm in the mining business, educated as a geologist & chemist. I like my SF hard, & I'm unco</span>
  <span id="freeText16545144716344204304" style="display:none">I'd been hesitant to read one of these, despite rave reviews by people I trust - I'm not much of a fantasy reader, &amp; we're talking vampires, zombies and werewolves here. Well, folks, what we *really* have is a book in the class of the Harold Shea books - one that bends genres and transcends them. I'm not even really going to review the book . . . .<br /><br />Let me back off a moment, &amp; tell you what I usually read. I'm in the mining business, educated as a geologist &amp; chemist. I like my SF hard, &amp; I'm uncomfortable with gore. So why would I like (let alone rave about) a vampire book with (literally) buckets of blood? Hint - it's probably not the scene where, as a joke, Anita tosses a cop the severed hand from a dismembered infant...<br /><br />It could be the scene where Anita (5'2", 102#) disarms a large rapist by sticking her derringer in his crotch &amp; threatening to blow his balls off...<br /><br />Anita's hard-boiled alright, but she's an uneasy executioner, a necromancer with scruples, even a soft touch sometimes - she tries to give a pretty prostitute a bus ticket out of town to "start over" (the whore laughs in her face). The gore is an integral part of the story, &amp; the supernatural is treated as just a part of everyday, late 20th C. life - as alternate history, really (I don't usually like alt hist either). I'm reminded somewhat of S.M. Stirling's Gwen in "The Drakon" (another <br />A+ book) - though Gwen is more cheerful at work. If nothing else, this one will lay to rest any lingering thoughts that women can't be as bloody-minded as men. Highly recommended.<br /><br />[Review written 1997; lightly revised 2019. My, how time flies!]</span>
  <a data-text-id="16545144716344204304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_81465611" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81465611" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81465611?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6583477-the-laughing-corpse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=necromancy">necromancy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81465611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7108707723988315108">After reading Guilty Pleasures and falling hook, line, and sinker into the Anita Blake world, I eagerly rushed forward to devour the second offering. The Laughing Corpse digs deeper into Blake’s world, shows off more of Jean-Claude, Ronnie, and the polices characters.<br/><br/>As always, Anita is surrounded by problems with no immediate, easy solution in sight. Emphasis isn’t placed heavily on her vampire slaying, more with her job as an animator. The suspense and story is strong from the beginning; actio</span>
  <span id="freeText7108707723988315108" style="display:none">After reading Guilty Pleasures and falling hook, line, and sinker into the Anita Blake world, I eagerly rushed forward to devour the second offering. The Laughing Corpse digs deeper into Blake’s world, shows off more of Jean-Claude, Ronnie, and the polices characters.<br /><br />As always, Anita is surrounded by problems with no immediate, easy solution in sight. Emphasis isn’t placed heavily on her vampire slaying, more with her job as an animator. The suspense and story is strong from the beginning; action begins immediately and never lets up. The ending is one of the strongest out of the series, nearly knocking me to the floor with its intensity.<br /><br />The voodoo priest as the villain is also one of my favorites out of every book. She’s dark, creepy, and as evil as they come – her showdowns with Anita were brilliant.<br /><br />Jean-Claude still isn’t shown much, which is a shame. The chemistry between him and Anita is amazing; Hamilton plays up on it heavily and it’s always thrilling to me, in more ways than one, to read their exchanges. This time around Jean-Claude wants something else from Anita (I won’t give away spoilers) and seeing her run from it is great fun.<br /><br />Hamilton consistently writes with a light, humorous hand while dealing with dark, depressing material. The characters she has written about are strong, unique in their own ways, and goal-driven.<br /><br />I enjoyed this one even more than the first – it keeps getting better, not an easy feat to pull off. I can’t find much fault with it, great stuff. The Anita Blakes are also rich in mystery; it somehow manages to come together at the end, remaining secretive and mysterious throughout the novel.<br /><br />The gore is pretty heavy, particularly the death scenes. Another big thumbs up for this book.<br /><br />A definite recommendation for a sequel just be sure to start at the beginning in order to keep up to date.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7108707723988315108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360604108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3926398792893272841">What a rush!!!<br/><br/>I'm officially part of the Anita Blake fan club. I would love to see this on TV (it would be terribly gory, even worse that The Walking Dead, I'd have to skip those parts, I have a weak stomach).<br/><br/>Anita Blake is once again in trouble, this time she has to deal with some kind of meat-eating zombie, she doesn't really know what it is, and she fears it may be the worst thing she will ever have to catch. This monster ate a family of three members, leaving only blood splattered everywhere</span>
  <span id="freeText3926398792893272841" style="display:none">What a rush!!!<br><br>I'm officially part of the Anita Blake fan club. I would love to see this on TV (it would be terribly gory, even worse that The Walking Dead, I'd have to skip those parts, I have a weak stomach).<br><br>Anita Blake is once again in trouble, this time she has to deal with some kind of meat-eating zombie, she doesn't really know what it is, and she fears it may be the worst thing she will ever have to catch. This monster ate a family of three members, leaving only blood splattered everywhere and a few half-eaten remains (yum!). <br>She also gets another job proposal, this time from a very dangerous man called Harold Gaynor, who offers her a million dollars to raise a 300-year-old corpse. However, to raise a dead body this old she must sacrifice a "white goat", aka a human being. Evidently she refuses to do so, as it breaks all moral codes she has. Gaynor doesn't take her refusal well. (let's keep it that way)<br>The third person who threatens Anita's life is the voodoo priestess Senora Dominga Salvador, a very dangerous woman who Anita suspects has had a hand in raising the zombie who's been murdering families. Dominga Salvador wishes to train her, to make Anita reach her true potential. Again, Anita refuses to have anything to do with her, especially after she sees what Dominga has hidden in her basement.<br>Also, there is still the remaining problem with vampire Master hottie, Jean-Claude who wants Anita to become his human slave. <br><br>Trust me guys, there a lot of wtf/mind-blowing moments...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298466ra/684232.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Again, I really enjoyed myself, LKH is a master at keeping me thoroughly addicted and at the same time completely grossed out. This series is definitely not your cup of tea if you don't like to read stuff about corpses getting eaten or ripped apart, as these kind of things tend to happen a lot. <br><br>All I can say is that I will keep reading, I can't stop now, I literally can't stop flipping the pages! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423830590ra/13679166.gif" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6654878-shannon?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400724084" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9742550712954953185">Caution: here be potty words! ;)<br/><br/><br/>Anita Blake books are always fun reads for me. I don't have to do any heavy thinking. I can just sit back and enjoy the ride. These books were written in the early '90s and I really enjoy reading about Anita's pager and how every time it goes off she has to race to find a pay phone! If that isn't enough, she actually wears a fanny pack in this book. How can you not love that?<br/><br/>I love Anita because she is so fucking kick ass! She knows her weapons, can kill things th</span>
  <span id="freeText9742550712954953185" style="display:none">Caution: here be potty words! ;)<br /><br /><br />Anita Blake books are always fun reads for me. I don't have to do any heavy thinking. I can just sit back and enjoy the ride. These books were written in the early '90s and I really enjoy reading about Anita's pager and how every time it goes off she has to race to find a pay phone! If that isn't enough, she actually wears a fanny pack in this book. How can you not love that?<br /><br />I love Anita because she is so fucking kick ass! She knows her weapons, can kill things that are already dead, tends to have bigger balls than all the men around her, and she is only 5'3!!! <br /><br />I love sarcasm, but sometimes Anita lays it on so thick that she comes off as a bitch, but I still love her.<br /><br />Zilch sex in this one, but a mega shit ton of gore!<br /><br />My one gripe is that Anita is 5'3, 106 pounds, AND has ginormous boobs! What the fuck are you smokin', LKH? More importantly, where can I get my hands on some of that shit? I hate to be a Debbie Downer here, but I think this may be a wee bit unrealistic...<br /><br /><br />***2019 REVIEW***<br /><br />Holy crap!! It's been seven years exactly since I last read this??? That's so weird and bizarre and totally unplanned so kinda creepy!!<br /><br />I still think this is a solid five stars. This series is just really entertaining, and I love it. Again, the audiobook is not my favorite, but I can get over that, especially since it made my last long car trip way more enjoyable than it would have been otherwise! </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_323220261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/323220261" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/323220261?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143144021" href="/book/show/6399684-the-laughing-corpse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=hello-my-name-is-mary-sue">hello-my-name-is-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=fashion-accident">fashion-accident</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer323220261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13889212681456091869">Anita Blake receives an offer to raise a 280 year old Zombie. But such a raising would require a human sacrifice, and Anita draws the line there. Dolph then summons her to the grisly scene of a crime--the remains of a family. Anita must now find the killer...before anyone else dies.<br/><br/>Even though I didn't care for either the novel or the graphic novel of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30281.Guilty_Pleasures__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___1_' title='Guilty Pleasures (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #1) by Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guilty Pleasures</a>, I decided to give this series another chance. I am glad I did, because this book was a lot more enjoyable than the previous book</span>
  <span id="freeText13889212681456091869" style="display:none">Anita Blake receives an offer to raise a 280 year old Zombie. But such a raising would require a human sacrifice, and Anita draws the line there. Dolph then summons her to the grisly scene of a crime--the remains of a family. Anita must now find the killer...before anyone else dies.<br /><br />Even though I didn't care for either the novel or the graphic novel of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30281.Guilty_Pleasures__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___1_" title="Guilty Pleasures (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #1) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Guilty Pleasures</a>, I decided to give this series another chance. I am glad I did, because this book was a lot more enjoyable than the previous book was.<br /><br />Anita Blake comes off far more likeable this time around. Sure, the chip on her shoulder threatens to devour her small frame, she could definitely use some anger management, and she has some views that seem a bit harsh (such as her angry tirade when a man wants to let his wife know what he will be doing late at night and how he is basically being pansy-whipped), but I at least cared about what happened to her. I also started to get some understanding of her background, of her beliefs, and of her struggles between what she does and how she justifies it to herself.<br /><br />The character list is much shorter this time around too, which helped me get more acquainted with some background characters. I continue to adore Ronnie, and I even have a new favorite character: Manny. That guy was totally awesome. Burt, Anita's boss, was bland, Gainer was pretty meh, Dominga was interesting (but I didn't like what happened to her), and Wheelchair Wanda wasn't too bad. Jean-Claude definitely has the sex appeal down pat, though I can't really say there was anything that really jumped out at me about him. He feels a lot like arm candy for Anita--he likes her because she hates him and that's where the Unresolved Sexual Tension comes from. Of course, there have been FAR WORSE male romantic interests out there, who have absolutely NO chemistry with the leading lady, so I don't want to give the impression that I despise him. Just that I can't see his purpose very clearly.<br /><br />One thing I didn't like about the characters was the racial stereotyping and the sexism. The male police officers sexually harass Anita--and no one does anything. Not acceptable. A Latina woman bemoans how Anita makes enough money to take care of herself and thus not make her want to find a man. All bodyguards are beefy and somewhat brainless; blondes tend to be stupid and airheads (unless they are Ronnie). After awhile, I wanted to start apologizing for their portrayal.<br /><br />The story this time around was told in a much cleaner, more traditional format that made it much easier for me to follow. Anita gets client, refuses offer. Police call her to scene, she starts to investigate. Makes sense. However, Anita still did very little investigating on the murder case. She did investigate why Gainer was after her, but that plotline almost dominated. In fact, Anita spent so much time on the Gainer plot that a total of THREE families were brutally murdered. Of course, her own life is important, but Anita spent WAY more time about something she WASN'T getting paid for. Seemed weird. She also spends WAY too much time yakking it up with Jean-Claude, getting him to explain the whole human servant thing and then having him escort her around the Tenderloin (which I couldn't help but snicker and yell, "STEAK!" at). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I so didn't care for how the killer Zombie ended up tying into the Gainer subplot. It almost felt like a children's book, where all the plots tie up neatly at the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The writing is serviceable, but certainly nothing to write home about. LKH has this tendency to latch onto certain words and repeat them over...and over...and over. Here are a few excerpts:<br /><br /><blockquote>"She had meant to <b>kill</b> me…Why <b>kill</b> me? I couldn't stop her legally; she knew that. So why make such a damned serious attempt to <b>kill</b> me? Dominga had given her word she hadn’t raised the <b>killer</b> zombie…she had something to do with the <b>killer</b> zombie…she’d raised the beast or why <b>kill</b> me the night after I talked to her?...She wouldn't just raise a <b>killer</b> zombie and let it loose."<br /><br />"He <b>stood</b> in front of me, hands at his sides. He <b>stood</b> very still. Snakes or birds can <b>stand</b> utterly still, but even a snake has a sense of aliveness...Jean-Claude <b>stood</b> there with no sense of anything."<br /><br />"I lifted the <b>hand</b> from the carpet...I wouldn't really have thrown the <b>hand</b>. I wouldn't. I cradled the tiny <b>hand</b> in my <b>hands</b>. It felt heavy, as if the fingers should curl around my <b>hand</b>...I dropped the <b>hand</b> on the carpet."<br /><br />“I decided to take the <b>beating</b>…I was going to get <b>beat</b> up, not pleasant, but I had made my mind up to take the <b>beating</b>…if my choices were A) getting <b>beat</b> up or B) performing human sacrifice, I’d take the <b>beating</b>.” </blockquote><br /><br />And then we have the gore. I didn't mention it last book because it wasn't that noteworthy, but this time around, WOWEE, there is a lot of blood and guts. We get description of at least THREE grisly death scenes and at least one has a child brutally mauled. We have Anita fighting, and she fights dirty at times. Do not read while eating or if you are mild of stomach.<br /><br />This is definitely an improvement over "Guilty Pleasures", which I thought was rambling and centered more on Anita avoiding death than investigating anything. Sure, this has loads of problems, but they are a quick read/listen and it wasn't too bad. I might check out a few more and see where to go from there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13889212681456091869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15273215142899130251">Note: this book is on my gruesome-horror shelf. Certain scene descriptions were disgusting and consequently depressing.<br/><br/>So far, this series is not what I expected. It is slightly grittier and not the least bit upbeat, but more along the lines of what I expect from quality dark urban-fantasy. I enjoyed this book more than the first, largely due to being more familiar with Hamilton's world and characters, something which is typical of long running series. The first books are usually the weakest. I </span>
  <span id="freeText15273215142899130251" style="display:none">Note: this book is on my gruesome-horror shelf. Certain scene descriptions were disgusting and consequently depressing.<br /><br />So far, this series is not what I expected. It is slightly grittier and not the least bit upbeat, but more along the lines of what I expect from quality dark urban-fantasy. I enjoyed this book more than the first, largely due to being more familiar with Hamilton's world and characters, something which is typical of long running series. The first books are usually the weakest. I desperately want to jump into book 3 but am pacing myself. Sadly, I know some of what happens in later books yet I think I have a good many to go before I encounter those which most reviewers claim started the downward trend into poor plotting and gratuitious sex. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3156547059" />
    <a title="Timothy Boyd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22819383-timothy-boyd"><img alt="Timothy Boyd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463955593p2/22819383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3156547059?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Timothy Boyd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Timothy Boyd" href="/user/show/22819383-timothy-boyd">Timothy Boyd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3156547059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1905082147712307729">It's hard for me not to compare these to Jim Butcher's Dresden Files books. There are alot of the same story frameworks and world settings. I know they came first and pretty much set the stage for Urban Fantasy to become a popular style of books. They are very good supernatural action/adventure/mystery stories. Nice action and flow throughout the book. I enjoy the, while somewhat dated well not to me, pop culture references. Recommended</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81655871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81655871" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81655871?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81655871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5185345115808332508">As I reread this series I am aware of just how much it has changed and mutated into something completely different from the original books. The Laughing Corpse is book #2 and focuses almost completely on Anita's zombie raising duties and her job helping the police on Spook Squad. This book is horribly gory and disturbing. I originally read it back before I had children and am relieved that I didn't attempt to read it when they were toddlers. That's all I'm sayin'.<br/><br/>In this book, Anita is called in</span>
  <span id="freeText5185345115808332508" style="display:none">As I reread this series I am aware of just how much it has changed and mutated into something completely different from the original books. The Laughing Corpse is book #2 and focuses almost completely on Anita's zombie raising duties and her job helping the police on Spook Squad. This book is horribly gory and disturbing. I originally read it back before I had children and am relieved that I didn't attempt to read it when they were toddlers. That's all I'm sayin'.<br /><br />In this book, Anita is called in to help with a murder investigation. A family has been attacked and it appears it is the work of some sort of up hyped up super zombie. While investigating the case Anita is being pressured to raise a long dead zombie for a million or so bucks. She refuses because she'd have to sacrifice a human in order to do so. This Anita has morals and she's sticking to them.<br /><br />There is a lot of action here but way too much description when it comes to Anita's guns (snore) and attire. Seriously, are there readers out there who really care what color the "swishies" are on her many pairs of Nike's? <br /><br />Jean-Claude makes a few appearances and attempts to seduce her with his other-worldly eyes and puffy shirts but this Anita still kills vamps and doesn't date them. Many characters are introduced here that I don't remember. Anita has quite a few girlfriends, sidekicks and co-workers who disappear in the later books. <br /><br />Despite my complaining I enjoyed this book quite a bit. It's very morbid but has the dark-edged wit that the later books are lacking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5185345115808332508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17101228487386890037">The Laughing Corpse is one of my least favorite AB books and I really don't know why. It's interesting, doesn't have all the sex craziness, no relationship drama but still... It doesn't have Edward either.<br/><br/>There is this one moment in the book that ruins it for me. Anita is, if nothing else, supposed to be the good guy(she says so herself many times) but in order to get what she wants from Wanda she lets JC terrify the poor woman. That's just wrong in my book.<br/><br/>Then we have the "Manny thing". I mean</span>
  <span id="freeText17101228487386890037" style="display:none">The Laughing Corpse is one of my least favorite AB books and I really don't know why. It's interesting, doesn't have all the sex craziness, no relationship drama but still... It doesn't have Edward either.<br><br>There is this one moment in the book that ruins it for me. Anita is, if nothing else, supposed to be the good guy(she says so herself many times) but in order to get what she wants from Wanda she lets JC terrify the poor woman. That's just wrong in my book.<br><br>Then we have the "Manny thing". I mean good guys are you know...good. They don't go around sacrificing people. Why does everything have to be so grey in this series? Black and white are nice colours to have as well.<br><br>Generally the book was good enough. I liked the Seniora a lot for a bad guy. She had all the right psychotic characteristics. I didn't like Gaynor though. He was greedy(too greedy) not crazy. Weird?               >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17444214202023236857">I found I was liking this a little more than the first one. I liked the first one, but with the second, I started liking Anita more, same with some of the other characters. She was likable so that was nice. Plus the plot was the main focus. Only two books in, but I'm liking the series. So far anyway. Hopefully the rest of the series is just as good. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2410631420" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2410631420" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33087263-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517436027p2/33087263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2410631420?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/33087263-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/7797359-the-laughing-corpse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33087263-brittany?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33087263-brittany?shelf=adult-fantasy">adult-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410631420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8122376425748202780">Anita Blake is back at it again. Raising zombies, killing vampires, working as a retainer for the Regional Preternatural Investigation Team, all while avoiding the Master Vampire of the City who happens to have the hots for her. You would think her life couldn't get more busy and complicated and you would be wrong. Now she is having altercations with the Voodoo Queen of St. Louis while trying to avoid a rich man who is willing to make any sacrifice to raise a zombie.<br/><br/>This was a reread for me, so </span>
  <span id="freeText8122376425748202780" style="display:none">Anita Blake is back at it again. Raising zombies, killing vampires, working as a retainer for the Regional Preternatural Investigation Team, all while avoiding the Master Vampire of the City who happens to have the hots for her. You would think her life couldn't get more busy and complicated and you would be wrong. Now she is having altercations with the Voodoo Queen of St. Louis while trying to avoid a rich man who is willing to make any sacrifice to raise a zombie.<br /><br />This was a reread for me, so I remembered the basics of the story, but it was still enjoyable. Anita Blake is still a tough as nails female who is clinging to her soul with all that she has, but it is only a matter of time until she falls for the Master Vampire, Jean Claude. The story was entertaining, although after having just visited New Orleans, I believe the representation of voodoo was very off. Definitely an enjoyable read and I will continue with rereading the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8122376425748202780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2074825029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5963636256244684004"><b>
  <i>***2017 Summer Lovin' Reading List***</i>
</b><br/><br/>How can I not adore a book that has a character bearing my name? May I say that I did love Wheelchair Wanda, the prostitute with a heart of gold? Even better, she lives while men die around her like flies!<br/><br/>But the book is about Anita, who is just a bit rougher and tougher that your average Urban Fantasy heroine. Because she is an animator/nercromancer, there are also far more zombies than I'm used to in the genre. How is it that I can lurve the vampires an</span>
  <span id="freeText5963636256244684004" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>***2017 Summer Lovin' Reading List***</i>
</b><br /><br />How can I not adore a book that has a character bearing my name? May I say that I did love Wheelchair Wanda, the prostitute with a heart of gold? Even better, she lives while men die around her like flies!<br /><br />But the book is about Anita, who is just a bit rougher and tougher that your average Urban Fantasy heroine. Because she is an animator/nercromancer, there are also far more zombies than I'm used to in the genre. How is it that I can lurve the vampires and feel so ambivalent about the zombies? I just don't understand their appeal.<br /><br />Nevertheless, Anita experiences what so many (if not all) UF heroines do--they suddenly find hidden depths to their powers which solves their current dilemma, but opens a whole can of worms, to be explored in further volumes. Has she found her leverage to use against Jean-Claude, the King of Vampires in her city, or will she be lulled into a false sense of safety with him? (I'm betting on door number two!)<br /><br />Right, off to order book three from my friendly neighbourhood public library!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5963636256244684004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6yypuM6wQ29vuLdj/FTvW7G4U4qVaNaOjofy88370pQIOnfQvqhWqUVqI1YPxfFLcqBjP+9DGuXLbm5xXKTIDw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yL6ooJdd+fj6/Wjb1LtWw5oh+yDtAtSQNE+NTnGrzTsrqHbI50XsPtAv/O4nKkjTWTnLlZcpGPtxphHM4PTXoA==')})
  }
//]]>
